2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen you use the \u003ccode\u003eSELECT\u003c/code\u003e statement to query data from a table, the order of rows in the result set is unspecified. To sort the rows in the result set, you add the \u003ccode\u003eORDER BY\u003c/code\u003e clause in the \u003ccode\u003eSELECT\u003c/code\u003e statement.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou can also specify the direction of the order by adding the command \u003ccode\u003eASC\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003eDESC\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"SELECT column1, column2, ...\nFROM tablename\nORDER BY columnname [ASC|DESC];\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSELECT\u003c/span\u003e column1, column2, ...\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eFROM\u003c/span\u003e tablename\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eORDER BY\u003c/span\u003e columnname [\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eASC\u003c/span\u003e|\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eDESC\u003c/span\u003e];\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eORDER BY\u003c/code\u003e clause in SQL allows you to sort the result set based on multiple columns. This is especially useful when you want to have a primary sort criterion and then a secondary sort criterion (and so on) for rows that have the same value in the primary sort column.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo sort the result set based on multiple columns:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"SELECT column1, column2, ...\nFROM tablename\nORDER BY columnname1 [ASC|DESC], columnname2 [ASC|DESC], ...;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSELECT\u003c/span\u003e column1, column2, ...\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eFROM\u003c/span\u003e tablename\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eORDER BY\u003c/span\u003e columnname1 [\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eASC\u003c/span\u003e|\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eDESC\u003c/span\u003e], columnname2 [\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eASC\u003c/span\u003e|\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eDESC\u003c/span\u003e], ...;\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen using multiple columns in the \u003ccode\u003eORDER BY\u003c/code\u003e clause:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe result set is first sorted by the first column.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf there are rows with duplicate values in the first column, the result set sorts those rows based on the second column, and so forth.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eExample:\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-example-3\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Example:\" 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e clause is an essential aspect of SQL, especially when you're working with aggregate functions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e clause groups rows that have the same values in specified columns into aggregate data, such as the sum, average, minimum, maximum, etc. It's often used with aggregate functions to perform an operation on each group of rows.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"SELECT column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)\nFROM tablename\nGROUP BY column1;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSELECT\u003c/span\u003e column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eFROM\u003c/span\u003e tablename\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/span\u003e column1;\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKey Points:\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-key-points\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Key Points:\" href=\"#key-points\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGrouping\u003c/strong\u003e: When using \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e, the data is divided into groups based on the values in the specified column(s). Each group represents one or more rows of the table.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAggregate Functions\u003c/strong\u003e: Once the data is grouped, you can use an aggregate function (like \u003ccode\u003eSUM\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eAVG\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eCOUNT\u003c/code\u003e, etc.) to perform a calculation on each group. The result is a single value per group.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMultiple Columns\u003c/strong\u003e: You can group by more than one column by listing multiple column names separated by commas. This creates groups based on the unique combinations of values in the specified columns.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eExample:\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-example-5\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Example:\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eNote that for the data we have this example doesn't make much sense, but this is how we would do it if we wanted to group by product and region.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen combined with other SQL clauses, the order of operation is essential:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e clause filters the rows on the given condition.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf there's a \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e clause, the filtered rows are then grouped.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAggregate functions are applied.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e clause filters the groups (if present) - we will explain this below.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eFinally, the \u003ccode\u003eORDER BY\u003c/code\u003e clause sorts the result set.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor instance, using the \u003ccode\u003esales\u003c/code\u003e table:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo get the total sales amount for each product in 2022:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"SELECT product, SUM(amount_sold) as total_sold\nFROM sales\nWHERE year = 2022\nGROUP BY product;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSELECT\u003c/span\u003e product, \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eSUM\u003c/span\u003e(amount_sold) \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eas\u003c/span\u003e total_sold\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eFROM\u003c/span\u003e sales\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eWHERE\u003c/span\u003e year \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e2022\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/span\u003e product;\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIn this example, the \u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e clause first filters out the records not from the year 2022. The remaining records are then grouped by product, and the total sales amount for each product is computed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eResulting Table\u003c/strong\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ctable\u003e\n\u003cthead\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003cth\u003eproduct\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003cth\u003etotal_sold\u003c/th\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/thead\u003e\n\u003ctbody\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003eLaptop\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e180\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003ctr\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003ePhone\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003ctd\u003e150\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eHAVING clause\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-having-clause\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: HAVING clause\" href=\"#having-clause\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e clause is a special clause in SQL that allows you to filter the result sets of a query after they have been grouped by a \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e clause. It's specifically used to filter aggregate results.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhile the \u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e clause filters rows before they're aggregated, the \u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e clause filters after the aggregation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"SELECT column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)\nFROM tablename\nGROUP BY column1\nHAVING condition;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSELECT\u003c/span\u003e column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eFROM\u003c/span\u003e tablename\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/span\u003e column1\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eHAVING\u003c/span\u003e condition;\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eKey Points:\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-key-points-2\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Key Points:\" href=\"#key-points-2\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePost-Aggregation Filtering\u003c/strong\u003e: The primary purpose of the \u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e clause is to allow filtering after the \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e operation. This is particularly useful when you want to include/exclude certain groups based on an aggregate criterion.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWorks with Aggregate Functions\u003c/strong\u003e: Conditions in the \u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e clause often involve aggregate functions like \u003ccode\u003eSUM()\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eAVG()\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eCOUNT()\u003c/code\u003e, etc.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNot a Substitute for WHERE\u003c/strong\u003e: It's important to note that \u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e isn't a replacement for the \u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e clause. Instead, they serve different purposes. If you need to filter individual rows before aggregation, use the \u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e clause.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eUsing the previously mentioned \u003ccode\u003esales\u003c/code\u003e table with columns \u003ccode\u003eproduct\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eregion\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eamount_sold\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003eyear\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo get products that have a total sold amount greater than 100:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"SELECT product, SUM(amount_sold) as total_sold\nFROM sales\nGROUP BY product\nHAVING total_sold \u0026gt; 100;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSELECT\u003c/span\u003e product, \u003cspan calculates the total amount sold for each product.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e clause then filters out groups (i.e., products) that have a total sold id=\"user-content-case-expression-in-sql\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: CASE Expression in SQL\" href=\"#case-expression-in-sql\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003eCASE\u003c/code\u003e expression provides a way to introduce conditional decision-making logic directly within SQL queries. It's akin to \"if-then-else\" logic in other programming languages.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"CASE\n    WHEN condition1 THEN result1\n    WHEN condition2 THEN result2\n    ...\n    ELSE result_else\nEND AS alias_name\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003eCASE\n    WHEN condition1 THEN result1\n    WHEN condition2 THEN result2\n    ...\n    ELSE result_else\nEND \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eAS\u003c/span\u003e alias_name\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWHEN\u003c/strong\u003e: Specifies a condition to check.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTHEN\u003c/strong\u003e: Provides the result to be returned if the condition is true.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eELSE\u003c/strong\u003e: (optional) Specifies the result to return if none of the \u003ccode\u003eWHEN\u003c/code\u003e conditions are met.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eEND\u003c/strong\u003e: Closes the \u003ccode\u003eCASE\u003c/code\u003e statement.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAS alias_name\u003c/strong\u003e: Gives a name to the new column formed as a result of the \u003ccode\u003eCASE\u003c/code\u003e expression.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eExample with the \u003ccode\u003esales\u003c/code\u003e table:\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-example-with-the-sales-table\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Example with the sales table:\" href=\"#example-with-the-sales-table\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eImagine we want to categorize products based on their 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eOrder of Writing SQL Clauses\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe order in which you write SQL clauses and the order in which they are executed by the database engine are two different things. This distinction is important for understanding how SQL processes your requests.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen constructing an SQL statement, the clauses need to be written in a specific order:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eSELECT\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eFROM\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eORDER BY\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eLIMIT\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"SELECT column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)\nFROM tablename\nWHERE condition_on_column\nGROUP BY column1\nHAVING condition_on_aggregated_column\nORDER BY column1\nLIMIT number;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eSELECT\u003c/span\u003e column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eFROM\u003c/span\u003e tablename\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eWHERE\u003c/span\u003e condition_on_column\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/span\u003e column1\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eHAVING\u003c/span\u003e condition_on_aggregated_column\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eORDER BY\u003c/span\u003e column1\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eLIMIT\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003enumber\u003c/span\u003e;\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eOrder of Execution of SQL Clauses\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe SQL engine does not execute clauses in the order they are written. Instead, it follows a specific sequence to process the data:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eFROM\u003c/code\u003e: It identifies the table(s) from which data is to be retrieved.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e: Filters the rows based on the condition specified. It acts on the result of the \u003ccode\u003eFROM\u003c/code\u003e clause.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e: It groups rows that have the same values in specified columns into aggregate data.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eHAVING\u003c/code\u003e: Filters the groups based on a condition. It acts on the result of the \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e clause.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eSELECT\u003c/code\u003e: Selects columns to be displayed in the final result. If there are any aggregate functions, they are computed here.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eORDER BY\u003c/code\u003e: Sorts the result set based on one or more columns.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eLIMIT\u003c/code\u003e: Limits the number of rows to be returned in the result set.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhy This Matters:\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-why-this-matters\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Why This Matters:\" href=\"#why-this-matters\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eUnderstanding the order of execution is crucial for several reasons:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePredictability\u003c/strong\u003e: Knowing how SQL processes the data helps you predict the outcome of your queries. For instance, the \u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e clause filters rows before they are grouped by the \u003ccode\u003eGROUP BY\u003c/code\u003e clause.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePerformance\u003c/strong\u003e: Optimizing the \u003ccode\u003eWHERE\u003c/code\u003e clause can significantly reduce the number of rows that need to be grouped, aggregated, or sorted in subsequent steps, leading to faster query performance.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDebugging\u003c/strong\u003e: If your query isn't returning what you expect, understanding the order of execution can help pinpoint where things are going awry.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eSummary\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-summary\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Summary\" href=\"#summary\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThis lesson introduces fundamental SQL commands and concepts essential for data retrieval and manipulation. You have seen how to use SELECT statements, aggregate functions, and the GROUP BY clause for organizing data, along with the WHERE and HAVING clauses for filtering data. The lesson also covers formatting numbers and dates with functions like FORMAT and DATE_FORMAT in MySQL. Additionally, you have learned various SQL operators for arithmetic, comparison, and logical operations. Finally you have seen that the order of writing and executing SQL clauses is crucial for optimized query performance and effective iZJewz"><nav data-testid="breadcrumbs" aria-labelledby="sticky-breadcrumb-heading" id="sticky-breadcrumb" class="Box-sc-g0xbh4-0 kzRgrI"><h2 class="Heading__StyledHeading-sc-1c1dgg0-0 cgQnMS sr-only" itemprop="text">
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Learning Objectives</h2><a id="user-content-learning-objectives" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Learning Objectives" href="#learning-objectives"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">By the end of this lesson, you will be able to:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Interpret tables by utilizing the <code>SELECT ... FROM</code> statement.</li>
<li>Identify and select <code>UNIQUE</code> values from a table.</li>
<li>Apply techniques to change the format of variables within a table.</li>
<li>Analyze data in a table and sort it using the <code>ORDER BY</code> clause.</li>
<li>Implement data aggregation in a table using the <code>GROUP BY</code> and <code>HAVING</code> clauses.</li>
<li>Demonstrate the ability to filter tables effectively using the <code>WHERE</code> clause.</li>
<li>Utilize various operators such as <code>IN</code>, <code>BETWEEN</code>, <code>LIKE</code>, <code>AND</code>, <code>OR</code>, <code>=</code>, <code>&gt;=</code> to manipulate and filter data.</li>
<li>Construct and apply conditions within SQL queries using the <code>CASE</code> statement.</li>
<li>Create new calculated variables for enhanced data analysis and manipulation.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Read tables with SELECT statement</h2><a id="user-content-read-tables-with-select-statement" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Read tables with SELECT statement" href="#read-tables-with-select-statement"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The most fundamental SQL command is the <code>SELECT</code> statement, which retrieves data from a database.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT * FROM tablename;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> <span class="pl-k">*</span> <span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This gets every row and column from the table <em>tablename</em>. The asterisk means "all the columns".</p>
<p dir="auto">If we want to select just a few columns we would do:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, column2
FROM tablename;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, column2
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Suppose we have a table <code>students</code> with columns <code>id</code>, <code>name</code>, and <code>age</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Table <code>students</code></strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>id</th>
<th>name</th>
<th>age</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>1</td>
<td>Alice</td>
<td>20</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2</td>
<td>Bob</td>
<td>22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3</td>
<td>Charlie</td>
<td>21</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4</td>
<td>David</td>
<td>23</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p dir="auto">To fetch all names from the <code>students</code> table:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT name FROM students;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> name <span class="pl-k">FROM</span> students;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Result</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>name</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Alice</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Bob</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Charlie</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>David</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Select only the UNIQUE values</h2><a id="user-content-select-only-the-unique-values" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Select only the UNIQUE values" href="#select-only-the-unique-values"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">When querying data from a table, you may get duplicate rows. To remove these duplicate rows (to get unique values in the output), you use the <code>DISTINCT</code> clause in the <code>SELECT</code> statement.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT DISTINCT columnname
FROM tablename;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT DISTINCT</span> columnname
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Table <code>students</code></strong> (same as above).To fetch unique ages from the <code>students</code> table:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT DISTINCT age FROM students;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT DISTINCT</span> age <span class="pl-k">FROM</span> students;</pre></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Aggregate functions</h2><a id="user-content-aggregate-functions" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Aggregate functions" href="#aggregate-functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To perform calculations on a set of values and return a single value, MySQL provides various aggregate functions like <code>COUNT()</code>, <code>SUM()</code>, <code>AVG()</code>, <code>MAX()</code>, and <code>MIN()</code>.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(columnname)
FROM tablename;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(columnname)
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-2" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-2"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Table <code>students</code></strong> (same as above).</p>
<p dir="auto">To find the average age of students:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT AVG(age) FROM students;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> <span class="pl-c1">AVG</span>(age) <span class="pl-k">FROM</span> students;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Result</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>AVG(age)</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>21.5</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">ORDER BY</h2><a id="user-content-order-by" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: ORDER BY" href="#order-by"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">When you use the <code>SELECT</code> statement to query data from a table, the order of rows in the result set is unspecified. To sort the rows in the result set, you add the <code>ORDER BY</code> clause in the <code>SELECT</code> statement.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can also specify the direction of the order by adding the command <code>ASC</code> or <code>DESC</code>.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, column2, ...
FROM tablename
ORDER BY columnname [ASC|DESC];"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, column2, ...
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename
<span class="pl-k">ORDER BY</span> columnname [<span class="pl-k">ASC</span>|<span class="pl-k">DESC</span>];</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The <code>ORDER BY</code> clause in SQL allows you to sort the result set based on multiple columns. This is especially useful when you want to have a primary sort criterion and then a secondary sort criterion (and so on) for rows that have the same value in the primary sort column.</p>
<p dir="auto">To sort the result set based on multiple columns:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, column2, ...
FROM tablename
ORDER BY columnname1 [ASC|DESC], columnname2 [ASC|DESC], ...;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, column2, ...
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename
<span class="pl-k">ORDER BY</span> columnname1 [<span class="pl-k">ASC</span>|<span class="pl-k">DESC</span>], columnname2 [<span class="pl-k">ASC</span>|<span class="pl-k">DESC</span>], ...;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">When using multiple columns in the <code>ORDER BY</code> clause:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>The result set is first sorted by the first column.</li>
<li>If there are rows with duplicate values in the first column, the result set sorts those rows based on the second column, and so forth.</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-3" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-3"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Table <code>students</code></strong>: same as before.</p>
<table>

<tr>
<th>id</th>
<th>name</th>
<th>age</th>
</tr>

<tbody>

<td>Alice</td>
<td>20</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2</td>
<td>Bob</td>
<td>22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3</td>
<td>Charlie</td>
<td>21</td>
</tr>

<td>4</td>
<td>David</td>
<td>23</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p dir="auto">To fetch all student names ordered by age in descending order:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT name FROM students ORDER BY age DESC;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> name <span class="pl-k">FROM</span> students <span class="pl-k">ORDER BY</span> age <span class="pl-k">DESC</span>;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In this case, the output will be sorted by age, so from the oldest to the youngest.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Result</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>name</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>David</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Bob</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Charlie</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Alice</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-4" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-4"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Suppose we have the <code>students</code> table, and we want to order the students primarily by their age and then, for students of the same age, alphabetically by name.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT name, age 
FROM students 
ORDER BY age DESC, name ASC;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> name, age 
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> students 
<span class="pl-k">ORDER BY</span> age <span class="pl-k">DESC</span>, name <span class="pl-k">ASC</span>;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In this example:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>The result set is first sorted in descending order by age.</li>
<li>For students who have the same age, their names are then sorted in ascending alphabetical order.</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">GROUP BY</h2><a id="user-content-group-by" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: GROUP BY" href="#group-by"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <code>GROUP BY</code> clause is an essential aspect of SQL, especially when you're working with aggregate functions.</p>
<p dir="auto">The <code>GROUP BY</code> clause groups rows that have the same values in specified columns into aggregate data, such as the sum, average, minimum, maximum, etc. It's often used with aggregate functions to perform an operation on each group of rows.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)
FROM tablename
GROUP BY column1;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> column1;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Key Points:</h3><a id="user-content-key-points" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Key Points:" href="#key-points"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Grouping</strong>: When using <code>GROUP BY</code>, the data is divided into groups based on the values in the specified column(s). Each group represents one or more rows of the table.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Aggregate Functions</strong>: Once the data is grouped, you can use an aggregate function (like <code>SUM</code>, <code>AVG</code>, <code>COUNT</code>, etc.) to perform a calculation on each group. The result is a single value per group.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Multiple Columns</strong>: You can group by more than one column by listing multiple column names separated by commas. This creates groups based on the unique combinations of values in the specified columns.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-5" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-5"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Let's consider a table named <code>sales</code> with columns <code>product</code>, <code>region</code>, <code>amount_sold</code>, and <code>year</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Table: sales</strong></p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>region</th>
<th>amount_sold</th>
<th>year</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>East</td>
<td>100</td>
<td>2022</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>150</td>
<td>2022</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>80</td>
<td>2022</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>North</td>
<td>90</td>
<td>2021</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>South</td>
<td>70</td>
<td>2021</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p dir="auto">If we want to determine the total sales amount for each product:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT product, SUM(amount_sold) as total_sold
FROM sales
GROUP BY product;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> product, <span class="pl-c1">SUM</span>(amount_sold) <span class="pl-k">as</span> total_sold
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> product;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>total_sold</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>270</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>220</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-6" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-6"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To ascertain the total sales amount for each product in every region:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT product, region, SUM(amount_sold) as total_sold
FROM sales
GROUP BY product, region;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> product, region, <span class="pl-c1">SUM</span>(amount_sold) <span class="pl-k">as</span> total_sold
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> product, region;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>region</th>
<th>total_sold</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>East</td>
<td>100</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>80</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>North</td>
<td>90</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>150</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>South</td>
<td>70</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p dir="auto">Note that for the data we have this example doesn't make much sense, but this is how we would do it if we wanted to group by product and region.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">WHERE clause for filtering data</h2><a id="user-content-where-clause-for-filtering-data" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: WHERE clause for filtering data" href="#where-clause-for-filtering-data"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <code>WHERE</code> clause is a fundamental part of SQL that allows you to filter records based on specific conditions, ensuring that only certain rows are selected or affected by a SQL statement.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, column2, ...
FROM tablename
WHERE condition;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, column2, ...
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename
<span class="pl-k">WHERE</span> condition;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Key Points:</h3><a id="user-content-key-points-1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Key Points:" href="#key-points-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Conditions</strong>: The condition in the <code>WHERE</code> clause can involve comparisons using operators like <code>=</code>, <code>&lt;&gt;</code> or <code>!=</code>, <code>&lt;</code>, <code>&gt;</code>, <code>&lt;=</code>, <code>&gt;=</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Logical Operators</strong>: You can combine multiple conditions using logical operators like <code>AND</code>, <code>OR</code>, and <code>NOT</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Functions and Expressions</strong>: The <code>WHERE</code> clause can also contain functions, arithmetic calculations, and other expressions.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-7" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-7"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Using the same <code>sales</code> table with columns <code>product</code>, <code>region</code>, <code>amount_sold</code>, and <code>year</code>:</p>

<p dir="auto">To fetch all sales records for the product "Laptop":</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT *

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example</h3><a id="user-content-example-8" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example" href="#example-8"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To fetch sales records for the product "Laptop" in the region "West" during the year 2022:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT * 
FROM sales
WHERE product = 'Laptop' AND region = 'West' AND year = 2022;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> <span class="pl-k">*</span> 
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales
<span class="pl-k">WHERE</span> product <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Laptop<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> <span class="pl-k">AND</span> region <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>West<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span> <span class="pl-k">AND</span> year <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">2022</span>;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>region</th>
<th>amount_sold</th>
<th>year</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>80</td>
<td>2022</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p dir="auto">When combined with other SQL clauses, the order of operation is essential:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>The <code>WHERE</code> clause filters the rows on the given condition.</li>
<li>If there's a <code>GROUP BY</code> clause, the filtered rows are then grouped.</li>
<li>Aggregate functions are applied.</li>
<li>The <code>HAVING</code> clause filters the groups (if present) - we will explain this below.</li>
<li>Finally, the <code>ORDER BY</code> clause sorts the result set.</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">For instance, using the <code>sales</code> table:</p>
<p dir="auto">To get the total sales amount for each product in 2022:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT product, SUM(amount_sold) as total_sold
FROM sales
WHERE year = 2022
GROUP BY product;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> product, <span class="pl-c1">SUM</span>(amount_sold) <span class="pl-k">as</span> total_sold
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales
<span class="pl-k">WHERE</span> year <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">2022</span>
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> product;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In this example, the <code>WHERE</code> clause first filters out the records not from the year 2022. The remaining records are then grouped by product, and the total sales amount for each product is computed.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>total_sold</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>180</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>150</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">HAVING clause</h2><a id="user-content-having-clause" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: HAVING clause" href="#having-clause"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <code>HAVING</code> clause is a special clause in SQL that allows you to filter the result sets of a query after they have been grouped by a <code>GROUP BY</code> clause. It's specifically used to filter aggregate results.</p>
<p dir="auto">While the <code>WHERE</code> clause filters rows before they're aggregated, the <code>HAVING</code> clause filters after the aggregation.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)
FROM tablename
GROUP BY column1
HAVING condition;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> column1
<span class="pl-k">HAVING</span> condition;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Key Points:</h3><a id="user-content-key-points-2" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Key Points:" href="#key-points-2"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Post-Aggregation Filtering</strong>: The primary purpose of the <code>HAVING</code> clause is to allow filtering after the <code>GROUP BY</code> operation. This is particularly useful when you want to include/exclude certain groups based on an aggregate criterion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Works with Aggregate Functions</strong>: Conditions in the <code>HAVING</code> clause often involve aggregate functions like <code>SUM()</code>, <code>AVG()</code>, <code>COUNT()</code>, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Not a Substitute for WHERE</strong>: It's important to note that <code>HAVING</code> isn't a replacement for the <code>WHERE</code> clause. Instead, they serve different purposes. If you need to filter individual rows before aggregation, use the <code>WHERE</code> clause.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example</h3><a id="user-content-example-9" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example" href="#example-9"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Using the previously mentioned <code>sales</code> table with columns <code>product</code>, <code>region</code>, <code>amount_sold</code>, and <code>year</code>:</p>
<p dir="auto">To get products that have a total sold amount greater than 100:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT product, SUM(amount_sold) as total_sold
FROM sales
GROUP BY product
HAVING total_sold &gt; 100;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> product, <span class="pl-c1">SUM</span>(amount_sold) <span class="pl-k">as</span> total_sold
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> product
<span class="pl-k">HAVING</span> total_sold <span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">100</span>;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In this example:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>The <code>GROUP BY</code> clause groups the sales by <code>product</code>.</li>
<li>The <code>SUM(amount_sold)</code> calculates the total amount sold for each product.</li>
<li>The <code>HAVING</code> clause then filters out groups (i.e., products) that have a total sold amount of 100 or less.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>total_sold</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>270</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Tablet</td>
<td>220</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Combining with WHERE:</h3><a id="user-content-combining-with-where" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Combining with WHERE:" href="#combining-with-where"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">You can use both <code>WHERE</code> and <code>HAVING</code> in the same query. Remember:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>WHERE</code> filters rows before aggregation.</li>
<li><code>HAVING</code> filters groups after aggregation.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">For instance:</p>
<p dir="auto">To get the total sales amount for each product in 2022, but only include those products with a total sold amount greater than 150:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT product, SUM(amount_sold) as total_sold
FROM sales
WHERE year = 2022
GROUP BY product
HAVING total_sold &gt; 150;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> product, <span class="pl-c1">SUM</span>(amount_sold) <span class="pl-k">as</span> total_sold
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales
<span class="pl-k">WHERE</span> year <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">2022</span>
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> product
<span class="pl-k">HAVING</span> total_sold <span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">150</span>;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In this example, the <code>WHERE</code> clause first filters out the records not from the year 2022. The remaining records are then grouped by product, the total sales amount for each product is computed, and finally, the <code>HAVING</code> clause filters out products that don't meet the sales threshold.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>total_sold</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>180</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">LIMIT Clause</h2><a id="user-content-limit-clause" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: LIMIT Clause" href="#limit-clause"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To limit the number of rows returned:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, column2, ...
FROM tablename
LIMIT number;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, column2, ...
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename
<span class="pl-k">LIMIT</span> <span class="pl-k">number</span>;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h3><a id="user-content-example-10" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-10"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To fetch the first three sales:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT * FROM sales LIMIT 3;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> <span class="pl-k">*</span> <span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales <span class="pl-k">LIMIT</span> <span class="pl-c1">3</span>;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>

<th>amount_sold</th>
<th>year</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>

<td>East</td>
<td>100</td>
<td>2022</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>150</td>
<td>2022</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>80</td>
<td>2022</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">CASE Expression in SQL</h2><a id="user-content-case-expression-in-sql" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: CASE Expression in SQL" href="#case-expression-in-sql"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <code>CASE</code> expression provides a way to introduce conditional decision-making logic directly within SQL queries. It's akin to "if-then-else" logic in other programming languages.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="CASE
    WHEN condition1 THEN result1
    WHEN condition2 THEN result2
    ...
    ELSE result_else
END AS alias_name"><pre>CASE
    WHEN condition1 THEN result1
    WHEN condition2 THEN result2
    ...
    ELSE result_else
END <span class="pl-k">AS</span> alias_name</pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>WHEN</strong>: Specifies a condition to check.</li>
<li><strong>THEN</strong>: Provides the result to be returned if the condition is true.</li>
<li><strong>ELSE</strong>: (optional) Specifies the result to return if none of the <code>WHEN</code> conditions are met.</li>
<li><strong>END</strong>: Closes the <code>CASE</code> statement.</li>
<li><strong>AS alias_name</strong>: Gives a name to the new column formed as a result of the <code>CASE</code> expression.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example with the <code>sales</code> table:</h3><a id="user-content-example-with-the-sales-table" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example with the sales table:" href="#example-with-the-sales-table"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Imagine we want to categorize products based on their <code>amount_sold</code>:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>High Sales: <code>amount_sold</code> greater than 200</li>
<li>Moderate Sales: <code>amount_sold</code> between 100 and 200</li>
<li>Low Sales: <code>amount_sold</code> less than 100</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Using the <code>sales</code> table with columns <code>product</code>, <code>region</code>, <code>amount_sold</code>, and <code>year</code>:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT product, region, amount_sold, year,
CASE 
    WHEN amount_sold &gt; 200 THEN 'High Sales'
    WHEN amount_sold &gt;= 100 AND amount_sold &lt;= 200 THEN 'Moderate Sales'
    ELSE 'Low Sales'
END AS sales_category
FROM sales;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> product, region, amount_sold, year,
CASE 
    WHEN amount_sold <span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">200</span> THEN <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>High Sales<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
    WHEN amount_sold <span class="pl-k">&gt;=</span> <span class="pl-c1">100</span> <span class="pl-k">AND</span> amount_sold <span class="pl-k">&lt;=</span> <span class="pl-c1">200</span> THEN <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Moderate Sales<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
    ELSE <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>Low Sales<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>
END <span class="pl-k">AS</span> sales_category
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In this example:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>The <code>CASE</code> expression evaluates each row's <code>amount_sold</code> value.</li>
<li>Depending on the value, it categorizes the sales as either 'High Sales', 'Moderate Sales', or 'Low Sales'.</li>
<li>The result of this categorization is displayed in a new column named <code>sales_category</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Given the <code>sales</code> table:</p>
<table>

</tr>

<td>2022</td>
</tr>

</tr>

<td>2021</td>
</tr>
