<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">FORMAT Function in SQL</h2><a id="user-content-format-function-in-sql" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: FORMAT Function in SQL" href="#format-function-in-sql"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <code>FORMAT</code> function is primarily used to format numbers and dates to make them more readable or to adhere to specific local or business conventions.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">1. <strong>Formatting Numbers</strong></h3><a id="user-content-1-formatting-numbers" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 1. Formatting Numbers" href="#1-formatting-numbers"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">In MySQL, the <code>FORMAT</code> function primarily formats numbers by grouping thousands and controlling the number of decimal places displayed.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Syntax</strong>:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="FORMAT(number, decimal_places, [locale])"><pre>FORMAT(<span class="pl-k">number</span>, decimal_places, [locale])</pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>number</strong>: The number to be formatted.</li>
<li><strong>decimal_places</strong>: The number of decimal places to be returned.</li>
<li><strong>locale</strong> (optional): The locale to be used for formatting (e.g., 'en_US').</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h4><a id="user-content-example-11" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-11"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To format the number 1234567.89 to two decimal places with a comma as the thousand separator:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT FORMAT(1234567.89, 2);  -- Returns '1,234,567.89'"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> FORMAT(<span class="pl-c1">1234567</span>.<span class="pl-c1">89</span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span>);  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">--</span> Returns '1,234,567.89'</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2. <strong>Formatting Dates</strong></h3><a id="user-content-2-formatting-dates" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2. Formatting Dates" href="#2-formatting-dates"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">While the <code>FORMAT</code> function in MySQL isn't used for date formatting, the <code>DATE_FORMAT</code> function is available for this purpose.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Syntax</strong>:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="DATE_FORMAT(date, format_specifiers)"><pre>DATE_FORMAT(<span class="pl-k">date</span>, format_specifiers)</pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>date</strong>: The date value to be formatted.</li>
<li><strong>format_specifiers</strong>: The format pattern using specific specifiers (e.g., <code>%Y</code> for year, <code>%m</code> for month, <code>%d</code> for day).</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Example:</h4><a id="user-content-example-12" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Example:" href="#example-12"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Assuming a table <code>sales</code> has a <code>sale_date</code> column:</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Table: sales with sale_date</strong></p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>product</th>
<th>region</th>
<th>amount_sold</th>
<th>sale_date</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Laptop</td>
<td>East</td>
<td>100</td>
<td>2022-06-15</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Phone</td>
<td>West</td>
<td>150</td>
<td>2022-09-20</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p dir="auto">If we want to format the date to display in the format "Month Day, Year", we can use:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT DATE_FORMAT(sale_date, '%M %d, %Y') AS formatted_date
FROM sales;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> DATE_FORMAT(sale_date, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>%M %d, %Y<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span>) <span class="pl-k">AS</span> formatted_date
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> sales;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Resulting Table</strong>:</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>formatted_date</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>June 15, 2022</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>September 20, 2022</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Considerations for Other Databases:</h3><a id="user-content-considerations-for-other-databases" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Considerations for Other Databases:" href="#considerations-for-other-databases"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>SQL Server</strong>: The <code>FORMAT</code> function can be used for both numbers and dates. For example, <code>FORMAT(some_date, 'yyyy-MM-dd')</code> to format a date.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Oracle</strong>: Oracle uses the <code>TO_CHAR</code> function for both number and date formatting. For instance, <code>TO_CHAR(some_date, 'YYYY-MM-DD')</code> for dates.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>PostgreSQL</strong>: PostgreSQL uses the <code>TO_CHAR</code> function similarly to Oracle for date and number formatting.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">SQL Operators</h2><a id="user-content-sql-operators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: SQL Operators" href="#sql-operators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">SQL operators are symbols or keywords used to perform operations on data in SQL queries. They help manipulate and compare data, filter rows, and perform calculations. Here are some common types of SQL operators:</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Arithmetic Operators:</h3><a id="user-content-arithmetic-operators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Arithmetic Operators:" href="#arithmetic-operators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>+</code> Addition</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>-</code> Subtraction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>*</code> Multiplication</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>/</code> Division</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>%</code> or <code>MOD</code> Modulus (division remainder)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Comparison Operators:</h3><a id="user-content-comparison-operators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Comparison Operators:" href="#comparison-operators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>=</code> Equal to</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>!=</code> or <code>&lt;&gt;</code> Not equal to</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>&lt;</code> Less than</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>&gt;</code> Greater than</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>&lt;=</code> Less than or equal to</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>&gt;=</code> Greater than or equal to</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Logical Operators:</h3><a id="user-content-logical-operators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Logical Operators:" href="#logical-operators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">AND: Logical AND</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">OR: Logical OR</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">NOT: Logical NOT</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Concatenation Operator:</h3><a id="user-content-concatenation-operator" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Concatenation Operator:" href="#concatenation-operator"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>||</code> or <code>CONCAT()</code>: Concatenates strings together</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Pattern Matching Operators:</h3><a id="user-content-pattern-matching-operators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Pattern Matching Operators:" href="#pattern-matching-operators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>LIKE</code>: Matches a pattern in text (supports wildcards)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>IN</code>: Checks if a value exists in a list of values</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">NULL Comparison Operators:</h3><a id="user-content-null-comparison-operators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: NULL Comparison Operators:" href="#null-comparison-operators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>IS NULL</code>: Checks if a value is NULL</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><code>IS NOT NULL</code>: Checks if a value is not NULL</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Between Operator:</h3><a id="user-content-between-operator" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Between Operator:" href="#between-operator"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>BETWEEN</code>: Checks if a value falls within a range</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Order of Writing and Executing SQL Clauses</h2><a id="user-content-order-of-writing-and-executing-sql-clauses" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Order of Writing and Executing SQL Clauses" href="#order-of-writing-and-executing-sql-clauses"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Order of Writing SQL Clauses</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">The order in which you write SQL clauses and the order in which they are executed by the database engine are two different things. This distinction is important for understanding how SQL processes your requests.</p>
<p dir="auto">When constructing an SQL statement, the clauses need to be written in a specific order:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li><code>SELECT</code></li>
<li><code>FROM</code></li>
<li><code>WHERE</code></li>
<li><code>GROUP BY</code></li>
<li><code>HAVING</code></li>
<li><code>ORDER BY</code></li>
<li><code>LIMIT</code></li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">For example:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-sql notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="SELECT column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)
FROM tablename
WHERE condition_on_column
GROUP BY column1
HAVING condition_on_aggregated_column
ORDER BY column1
LIMIT number;"><pre><span class="pl-k">SELECT</span> column1, AGGREGATE_FUNCTION(column2)
<span class="pl-k">FROM</span> tablename
<span class="pl-k">WHERE</span> condition_on_column
<span class="pl-k">GROUP BY</span> column1
<span class="pl-k">HAVING</span> condition_on_aggregated_column
<span class="pl-k">ORDER BY</span> column1
<span class="pl-k">LIMIT</span> <span class="pl-k">number</span>;</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Order of Execution of SQL Clauses</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">The SQL engine does not execute clauses in the order they are written. Instead, it follows a specific sequence to process the data:</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li><code>FROM</code>: It identifies the table(s) from which data is to be retrieved.</li>
<li><code>WHERE</code>: Filters the rows based on the condition specified. It acts on the result of the <code>FROM</code> clause.</li>
<li><code>GROUP BY</code>: It groups rows that have the same values in specified columns into aggregate data.</li>
<li><code>HAVING</code>: Filters the groups based on a condition. It acts on the result of the <code>GROUP BY</code> clause.</li>
<li><code>SELECT</code>: Selects columns to be displayed in the final result. If there are any aggregate functions, they are computed here.</li>
<li><code>ORDER BY</code>: Sorts the result set based on one or more columns.</li>
<li><code>LIMIT</code>: Limits the number of rows to be returned in the result set.</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Why This Matters:</h3><a id="user-content-why-this-matters" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Why This Matters:" href="#why-this-matters"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Understanding the order of execution is crucial for several reasons:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Predictability</strong>: Knowing how SQL processes the data helps you predict the outcome of your queries. For instance, the <code>WHERE</code> clause filters rows before they are grouped by the <code>GROUP BY</code> clause.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Performance</strong>: Optimizing the <code>WHERE</code> clause can significantly reduce the number of rows that need to be grouped, aggregated, or sorted in subsequent steps, leading to faster query performance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Debugging</strong>: If your query isn't returning what you expect, understanding the order of execution can help pinpoint where things are going awry.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Summary</h2><a id="user-content-summary" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Summary" href="#summary"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">This lesson introduces fundamental SQL commands and concepts essential for data retrieval and manipulation. You have seen how to use SELECT statements, aggregate functions, and the GROUP BY clause for organizing data, along with the WHERE and HAVING clauses for filtering data. The lesson also covers formatting numbers and dates with functions like FORMAT and DATE_FORMAT in MySQL. Additionally, you have learned various SQL operators for arithmetic, comparison, and logical operations. Finally you have seen that the order of writing and executing SQL clauses is crucial for optimized query performance and effective debugging.</p>
